SCENARIO6_EXTRA_DOCUMENTATION_START
scenario6_doc_line_1=Scenario 6 is the privacy-preserving training scenario.
scenario6_doc_line_2=The fixed elements are dataset, clients, base class, target class, and poison fraction.
scenario6_doc_line_3=The changing element is privacy level.
scenario6_doc_line_4=The privacy mechanism is clipping plus Gaussian server noise.
scenario6_doc_line_5=The compared privacy levels are none, low, medium, and high.
scenario6_doc_line_6=The main empirical output is Poison Acc under each privacy level.
scenario6_doc_line_7=The secondary empirical output is Val Acc under each privacy level.
scenario6_doc_line_8=The privacy-budget value is only a proxy, not formal epsilon accounting.
scenario6_doc_line_9=The purpose is to test whether privacy-preserving noise weakens backdoors.
scenario6_doc_line_10=If Poison Acc decreases with privacy level, privacy helps against the backdoor.
scenario6_doc_line_11=If Val Acc decreases too much, privacy hurts normal performance.
scenario6_doc_line_12=Dirty-label and clean-label attacks are both evaluated.
scenario6_doc_line_13=Dirty-label should show labels_changed equal to poisoned_samples.
scenario6_doc_line_14=Clean-label should show labels_changed equal to zero.
scenario6_doc_line_15=The same privacy settings are used for dirty and clean runs.
scenario6_doc_line_16=The run name includes privnone, privlow, privmedium, or privhigh.
scenario6_doc_line_17=The privacy mode can be none, clip_only, noise_only, or clip_noise.
scenario6_doc_line_18=The main thesis version uses clip_noise.
scenario6_doc_line_19=The aggregation file prints proof that noise/clipping are active.
scenario6_doc_line_20=This scenario is separate from the broad defense comparison scenario.
SCENARIO6_EXTRA_DOCUMENTATION_END
